For each topic, we lay out the available partitions in numeric order\\n44:  * and the consumers in lexicographic order. We then divide the number of partitions by the total number of\\n45:  * consumers to determine the number of partitions to assign to each consumer. If it does not evenly\\n46:  * divide, then the first few consumers will have one extra partition.\\n47:  *\\n48:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and\\n49:  * <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>,\\n50:  * <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\\n51:  *\\n52:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n53:  * <ul>\\n54:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n55:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code></li>\\n56:  * </ul>\\n57:  *\\n58:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\\n59:  * For the above example, after one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\\n60:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C2</code>.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n63:  * <ul>\\n64:  * <li><code>C3 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1])</code>\\n65:  * <li><code>C2 (was C1): [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\\n66:  * </ul>\\n67:  *\\n68:  * The assignment change was caused by the change of <code>member.id</code> relative order, and\\n69:  * can be avoided by setting the group.instance.id.\\n70:  * Consumers will have individual instance ids <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>. As long as\\n71:  * 1. Number of members remain the same across generation\\n72:  * 2. Static members' identities persist across generation\\n73:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\\n74:  *\\n75:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\\n76:  * <ul>\\n77:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code>\\n78:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\\n79:  * </ul>\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Rack-aware assignment is used if both consumer and partition replica racks are available and\\n82:  * some partitions have replicas only on a subset of racks. We attempt to match consumer racks with\\n83:  * partition replica racks on a best-effort basis, prioritizing balanced assignment over rack alignment.\\n84:  * Topics with equal partition count and same set of subscribers guarantee co-partitioning by prioritizing\\n85:  * co-partitioning over rack alignment. In this case, aligning partition replicas of these topics on the\\n86:  * same racks will improve locality for consumers. For example, if partitions 0 of all topics have a replica\\n87:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 on rack 'b' etc., partition 0 of all topics can be assigned to a consumer\\n88:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 to a consumer on rack 'b' and so on.\\n89:  * <p>\\n90:  * Note that rack-aware assignment currently takes all replicas into account, including any offline replicas\\n91:  * and replicas that are not in the ISR. This is based on the assumption that these replicas are likely\\n92:  * to join the ISR relatively soon. Since consumers don't rebalance on ISR change, this avoids unnecessary\\n93:  * cross-rack traffic for long durations after replicas rejoin the ISR. In the future, we may consider\\n94:  * rebalancing when replicas are added or removed to improve consumer rack alignment.\\n95:  * </p>\\n96:  */\\n97: public class RangeAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\\n98:     public static final String RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \\\"range\\\";\\n99:     private static final TopicPartitionComparator PARTITION_COMPARATOR = new TopicPartitionComparator();\\n100: \\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/RangeAssignor.java%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5edcb83d-830f-41cd-9712-c033547c9348","uuid":"c8ee67b2-a880-46e6-98af-78db29a12d4d","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\\n3:  * contributor license agreements. For each topic, we lay out the available partitions in numeric order\n44:  * and the consumers in lexicographic order. We then divide the number of partitions by the total number of\n45:  * consumers to determine the number of partitions to assign to each consumer. If it does not evenly\n46:  * divide, then the first few consumers will have one extra partition.\n47:  *\n48:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and\n49:  * <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>,\n50:  * <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\n51:  *\n52:  * <p>The assignment will be:\n53:  * <ul>\n54:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\n55:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code></li>\n56:  * </ul>\n57:  *\n58:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\n59:  * For the above example, after one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\n60:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C2</code>.\n61:  *\n62:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\n63:  * <ul>\n64:  * <li><code>C3 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1])</code>\n65:  * <li><code>C2 (was C1): [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\n66:  * </ul>\n67:  *\n68:  * The assignment change was caused by the change of <code>member.id</code> relative order, and\n69:  * can be avoided by setting the group.instance.id.\n70:  * Consumers will have individual instance ids <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>. As long as\n71:  * 1. Number of members remain the same across generation\n72:  * 2. Static members' identities persist across generation\n73:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\n74:  *\n75:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\n76:  * <ul>\n77:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code>\n78:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\n79:  * </ul>\n80:  * <p>\n81:  * Rack-aware assignment is used if both consumer and partition replica racks are available and\n82:  * some partitions have replicas only on a subset of racks. We attempt to match consumer racks with\n83:  * partition replica racks on a best-effort basis, prioritizing balanced assignment over rack alignment.\n84:  * Topics with equal partition count and same set of subscribers guarantee co-partitioning by prioritizing\n85:  * co-partitioning over rack alignment. In this case, aligning partition replicas of these topics on the\n86:  * same racks will improve locality for consumers. For example, if partitions 0 of all topics have a replica\n87:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 on rack 'b' etc., partition 0 of all topics can be assigned to a consumer\n88:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 to a consumer on rack 'b' and so on.\n89:  * <p>\n90:  * Note that rack-aware assignment currently takes all replicas into account, including any offline replicas\n91:  * and replicas that are not in the ISR. This is based on the assumption that these replicas are likely\n92:  * to join the ISR relatively soon. Since consumers don't rebalance on ISR change, this avoids unnecessary\n93:  * cross-rack traffic for long durations after replicas rejoin the ISR. In the future, we may consider\n94:  * rebalancing when replicas are added or removed to improve consumer rack alignment.\n95:  * </p>\n96:  */\n97: public class RangeAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\n98:     public static final String RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \"range\";\n99:     private static final TopicPartitionComparator PARTITION_COMPARATOR = new TopicPartitionComparator();\n100: \n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/RangeAssignor.java%3FL1-100"}}}

<li<code>    M0: [T1P0, T1P1, T2P0, T2P1]    </code></li>\\n57:  * <li><code>   M1: [T1P2, T2P2]                </code></li>\\n58:  * </ul>\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>member.instance.id</code> to make the\\n61:  * assignment behavior more sticky.\\n62:  * For the above example, after one rolling bounce, the group coordinator will attempt to assign new member Ids towards\\n63:  * members, for example if <code>M0</code> -&gt; <code>M3</code> <code>M1</code> -&gt; <code>M2</code>.\\n64:  *\\n65:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n66:  * <ul>\\n67:  * <li><code>   M3 (was M0): [T1P2, T2P2]               (before it was [T1P0, T1P1, T2P0, T2P1])  </code>\\n68:  * <li><code>   M2 (was M1): [T1P0, T1P1, T2P0, T2P1]   (before it was [T1P2, T2P2])  </code>\\n69:  * </ul>\\n70:  *\\n71:  * The assignment change was caused by the change of <code>member.id</code> relative order, and\\n72:  * can be avoided by setting the instance.id.\\n73:  * Members will have individual instance Ids <code>I0</code>, <code>I1</code>. As long as\\n74:  * 1. Number of members remain the same.\\n75:  * 2. Topic metadata doesn't change.\\n76:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member.\\n77:  *\\n78:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\\n79:  * <ul>\\n80:  * <li><code>   I0: [T1P0, T1P1, T2P0, T2P1]    </code>\\n81:  * <li><code>   I1: [T1P2, T2P2]                </code>\\n82:  * </ul>\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  */\\n85: public class RangeAssignor implements ConsumerGroupPartitionAssignor {\\n86:     public static final String NAME = \\\"range\\\";\\n87: \\n88:     @Override\\n89:     public String name() {\\n90:         return NAME;\\n91:     }\\n92: \\n93:     /**\\n94:      * Metadata for a topic including partition and subscription details.\\n95:      */\\n96:     private static class TopicMetadata {\\n97:         private final Uuid topicId;\\n98:         private final int numPartitions;\\n99:         private int numMembers;\\n100:         private int minQuota = -1;\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/assignor/RangeAssignor.java%3FL1-100\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /*\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\n3:  * contributor license agreements.
